Local News

Memorial Service for Fallen Soldiers Held Today 77

▲ Zhang Qun Presides, Xu Jinyuan Assists

▲ Judicial and Administrative Agencies on Holiday

Various agencies and organizations in the city decided to hold a memorial service for the fallen soldiers who died suppressing the rebellion at the public stadium at 8:00 AM today. Mayor Zhang Qun was publicly recommended to preside over the ceremony, and Chief of Staff Xu Jinyuan of the Songhu Garrison Command was recommended to assist. The following procedures for the ceremony were decided: (1) Thirty-three gun salutes; (2) All stand at attention; (3) Play mourning music; (4) Bow three times to the Party, National Flag, Sun Yat-sen’s portrait, and fallen soldiers; (5) The chairperson respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will; (6) Three minutes of silence; (7) Present flowers; (8) Read eulogy; (9) The highest-ranking official delivers a speech; (10) Representatives from various agencies deliver speeches; (11) Speech; (12) All shout slogans; (13) Play mourning music; (14) Ceremony concludes; (15) Close on the 12th, the rituals are the same as those of a regular meeting, except that there are no gun salutes and no reading of the eulogy.

The various administrative and judicial agencies in the city received a long-distance telephone call from the capital yesterday stating that the 10th of this month is Memorial Day for Fallen Soldiers and that they should take a day off to rest. A public announcement was immediately made to inform everyone.

All post offices in the city are closed today due to the holiday, except for the postal savings department, money order department, and parcel department, which will be closed all day. The rest will follow the usual Sunday schedule.

Confirmed News of the Northeast Paper Mill 82

▲ Situation As Spoken by Preparatory Office Director Jin Han

Jin Han, the director of the Northeast Paper Mill Preparatory Office, recently came to Shanghai from Shenyang. The reporter visited his residence yesterday and learned more details about the preparation of the factory. The following is a summary of what he said to inform the readers. The Northeast Paper Mill was advocated by Deputy Commander-in-Chief Zhang, who, despite being very busy with government affairs, also pays great attention to industry. Recently, in view of the excellent forests in the eastern provinces and the urgent need for paper, he deeply desires to establish a state-of-the-art paper mill to recover economic rights and benefit culture. Therefore, last spring, he invited Mr. Jin to go north to investigate suitable locations for establishing a newspaper mill. Later, Mr. Jin, together with Mr. Zhao Jinglong, went to the upper reaches of the Songhua River for investigation and selected Pizhou in Liangdian County, Jilin, as the site of the paper mill, and the Lao'e River, 20 miles away, as the site of the hydroelectric power plant. The area is rich in timber, which is suitable for manufacturing newsprint. The terrain and water volume are suitable for building a dam to generate electricity, and transportation is convenient due to the completion of the Shenhai Railway a year ago. In addition, clear water and minerals such as coal, sulfur, and limestone are all available. After Mr. Jin and others reported, Mr. Zhang was satisfied and decided to raise huge funds to build a state-of-the-art, perfect newsprint mill, adopting the methods of large-scale and highly efficient newsprint mills in the West to manufacture newsprint. In early October, a preparatory office was established outside the Dabeibian Gate on Central Road in Shenyang, with Mr. Zhang Zhiliang appointed as the director, Mr. Jin as the director, and Mr. Zhao as the deputy director. Together, they discussed methods and actively proceeded. Surveying engineers were borrowed from the North China Water Conservancy Commission in Tianjin, and rock drilling workers were borrowed from the Jinkou Coal Mine Company, and they went to Pizhou Lao'e River to measure the paper mill and dam base and hydrology, and to drill and test the rocks at the bottom of the river. The measurement has been completed, and the rock drilling is still in progress. Once all the preliminary work is completed, preparations will be made to purchase machinery. The factory has many advantages and will definitely be profitable. The capital required is very large, and all parties are welcome to invest. The smoothness of the progress this time is largely due to the support of the local people, with Wang Shuhan, Wu Jiaxiang, Qian Jechen, Peng Jiqun, and others being particularly helpful. Zhang Zhiliang is a major industrialist in Liaoning and once served as the chairman of the Fengtian General Chamber of Commerce and the chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce. He is currently the general manager of the Shenhai Railway Company. Mr. Jin specialized in papermaking at the papermaking department of the University of Maine in the United States and received a master's degree. He also served as an intern technician at the Great Northern Paper Company and the Conserved Pulpwood Company in the United States for more than four years. After returning to China, he served as a technician at the Guangxi Construction Department and an investigator specially appointed by the Zhejiang Provincial Government, handling the investigation of forest water resources and the design of paper mills. Mr. Zhao graduated from the Department of Applied Chemistry of Osaka Higher Industrial School in Japan and interned at a Japanese paper mill for more than a year. The three men are knowledgeable and experienced, and Deputy Commander-in-Chief Zhang is very enthusiastic in presiding over the project, so the future is full of hope.

Cotton Mill Federation Telegraphs to Cancel Hebei Cotton Tax 88

The China Cotton Mill Federation telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry a few days ago, stating: "The president of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, the Minister of Finance, and the Minister of Industry: Previously, the Tianjin Cotton Mill Association telegraphed that after Hebei levied a unified tax on cotton yarn, the tax on cotton was still levied as usual. After receiving the telegram from the affiliated association, it believed that Hebei was still levying cotton yarn after the abolition of the likin tax, which was illegal. It telegraphed your ministry to stop it or issue the refund from the unified tax on cotton yarn. Later, Dong Dai replied in a telegram that the regulations on the unified tax on cotton yarn did not provide for the refund of the cotton tax. Upon receiving this, we were extremely puzzled. The focus of this case is whether the cotton tax in Hebei should be levied or not, not whether the cotton yarn should be refunded. If it is said that the regulations on the unified tax on cotton yarn do not provide for the refund of the cotton tax, and the illegal cotton tax in Hebei is completely ignored, it is one thing to abolish the likin tax, and another to tacitly approve Hebei's disguised likin tax, and yet another to collect a unified tax on cotton yarn in the name of compensating for the abolition of the likin tax. If the government is to show the country its good faith, it would not contradict itself to this extent. We urge you to quickly telegram the Hebei Provincial Government to cancel the cotton tax likin as soon as possible in order to preserve credibility and relieve the difficulties of merchants. We await your urgent order, China Cotton Mill Federation."

Requests from Various Industries for Exemption or Reduction of Business Tax 89

▲ Textile Industry The Shanghai Textile Industry Association sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, stating: “Regarding the Ministry of Finance’s promulgation of the Outline for the Collection of Business Tax: Business tax is a local revenue source, as stated in Article 1; provinces should determine tax rates based on local commercial conditions, as stated in Article 2; and all taxes of the same nature should be abolished, as stated in Article 7. Our textile industry was instructed by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on June 22nd of the 17th year of the Republic of China to follow the National Government’s resolution that handmade textiles, being a major domestic product, should be exempt from tax and levies according to the precedent of the 7th year of the Republic, based on six standard rules, to promote sales and maintain the livelihoods of the poor who are both producers and consumers. This instruction is on file. Before the abolition of levies, the government had no such revenue. Now that taxes and levies have been abolished, there seems to be no need to compensate for the textile industry. While handmade textiles do not entirely align with the principle of non-profit, it is necessary to study and maintain their role in assisting the development of various local businesses. Historically, there were three industries that fundamentally benefited the people: (1) pawnshops, (2) rice businesses, and (3) handmade textiles. Exchanging cloth for money and money for grain enables farmers to have surplus grain and women to have surplus cloth. This is a request for people's livelihood from thousands of years of history. Cotton is spun into yarn, and yarn is made into cloth. Now, cotton is collected by factories, and yarn comes from factories, so the tax has already been levied at the source. The National Government recognizes this and stipulates that cotton yarn that has already paid the consolidated tax is not subject to double taxation when directly woven into goods (see Article 5 of the Consolidated Tax Regulations). Considering the government’s decade of effort in maintaining this, we naturally request exemption. From the perspective of the commercial people's burden, the textile industry benefits the people, and the loom operators are all poor, unable to support themselves and are on the verge of closing down. How can we console the late Premier's emphasis on people's livelihood, and how can we secure the livelihoods of tens of millions of poor people? Our association and the loom operators are interdependent. We are not crying wolf. We are concerned for the city and the countryside, hoping to preserve this lifeline and prevent foreign goods from flooding the market and regaining their dominance. We respectfully submit this letter explaining the reasons for exempting our industry's textiles to your esteemed association for review and submission to the authorities, requesting approval for exemption. We would be extremely grateful.”

▲ Lace Industry The Shanghai Lace and Embroidery Trade Association telegraphed the Central Executive Committee, the National Government Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry, stating: “Our association's lace and embroidery industry has historically been exempt from customs duties and levies. We now request that it remain exempt from business tax in order to maintain the established precedent and align with the principle of encouraging foreign trade. We have appointed Yi Deng and others, elected at the public meeting on February 20th, as representatives to submit petitions to your esteemed committees, yuan, and ministries, requesting approval to issue a nationwide order to exempt lace and embroidery from business tax. We are immensely grateful that your esteemed committees, yuan, and ministries have agreed to adopt our request. We should await the official reply in silence and dare not make further statements. However, there are still omissions in the four reasons listed in the original petition. Therefore, we specifically submit four additional reasons by telegram for your kind consideration. The term 'lace' in the market actually distinguishes between the lace industry and the lace embroidery industry. When our association submitted the petition in Nanjing, we submitted samples of tablecloths, placemats, and handkerchiefs produced by our members. Some are made with sand yarn, and others have embroidered patterns surrounded by lace. These are customarily referred to as lace, but they are actually household necessities such as large and small tablecloths, dining table cloths, hand towels, piano covers, chair cushions, placemats, and pillowcases. To simplify identification, our members named it lace embroidery. At the same time, we also submitted three samples of foreign-made lace used to decorate women's clothing. The representatives explained the differences in person, and all were accepted for review. We believe that your esteemed committees, yuan, and ministries, with your keen insight, will be able to understand the details. However, lace is a product manufactured overseas and sold in China, while lace embroidery involves our members receiving orders for fabric from foreign merchants and distributing it to poor women for needlework before delivering it to foreign merchants. The nature is completely different. Considering the government's historical policy of exempting taxes and levies to promote development, and following the common practice of modern countries in protecting tariffs, the lace embroidery industry should not be subject to business tax. This is the first reason for requesting a clear exemption. The business tax regulations promulgated by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments only list lace in the schedule of taxable goods in the commodity sales industry, with a tax rate of 20 per mille. Lace embroidery does not have a clearly defined tax rate. The intention behind this may be to encourage and promote the development of domestic handicrafts that only trade with foreign countries. However, since lace and lace embroidery are both commonly referred to as lace in the market, if there is no clear distinction at this time, we fear that the confusion in names may lead to misunderstandings when collecting taxes in the future. This is the second reason for requesting a clear exemption. Some argue that business tax is a direct tax, and unless otherwise stipulated in Article 1 of the Outline Supplementary Measures, all businesses should fulfill their obligation to pay taxes. The lace embroidery industry's request for exemption seems to lack a legal basis. If the government authorities approve this request, other industries will follow suit, making it difficult to handle. However, those who say this have not fully considered the matter. All industries used to have customs duties and levies, so business tax must be collected to compensate for this. However, the lace embroidery industry has not had any levies for over 40 years, so there is no loss from the abolition of levies, and there is no need to consider compensation. The argument of following suit is an overconcern. Even if it is said that the textile industry, which was also exempt from taxes and levies, must now pay business tax, lace embroidery seems to be an exception. However, their natures are not entirely the same. Lace embroidery involves receiving orders for fabric from foreign merchants, having it made by women's handicrafts, and then selling it overseas without any domestic sales. In reality, our members only earn a small commission from foreign merchants to make a living, and poor women rely on this to survive. Although the textile industry is also a handicraft, its products are mostly sold in various parts of the country. The situations are so different that there is no basis for following suit. This is the third reason for requesting a clear exemption. The central government's determination to abolish levies is intended to promote the development of domestic industries and to seek the prosperity of domestic commerce. However, since levies are a major source of tax revenue for our country, it is inevitable that alternative ways to compensate for the loss must be found during this time when the national treasury is strained. The business tax is intended to compensate for local losses from the abolition of levies, which is also a reluctant measure. The lace embroidery industry was supported and encouraged by the government during the era of harsh levies, with exemptions from customs duties and levies. Now that levies have been abolished nationwide and industries are celebrating their recovery, it would be contrary to the central government's intention to abolish levies and the government's desire to benefit businesses and people if the lace embroidery industry were subjected to business tax. Furthermore, the lace embroidery industry is already affected by the decline in foreign markets and is under pressure from government-subsidized competition from countries such as Portugal and Japan. It is impossible for businesses to bear this burden. This is the fourth reason for requesting a clear exemption.” (Xia Yu)

▲ Tea and Snack Industry The Tea and Snack Industry Association sent a letter to the Tax Regulations Research Committee of various industry associations, stating: “Regarding the business tax regulations promulgated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, our association is included in the highest tax bracket, with a tax rate of 20 per mille, which is more than ten times higher than the rate set by the Ministry. The merchants are all extremely alarmed. The establishment of our stores has always been characterized by small-scale operations with small capital and minor business. The products sold are mostly pastries and cakes, without wholesale business. All sales are retail, and the operating profit is meager, like flies' heads. We have always had a poor profession. In prosperous years, we can still make a living, but in years of commercial depression, we cannot even cover our expenses. Furthermore, the raw materials used, such as sugar, oil, rice, and flour, have already been taxed when purchased. If we are taxed again at such a high rate after processing them into finished products, it is not only beyond our ability but also lacks legal basis. The reasons for requesting a lower rate are as follows: (1) Tea and snacks are actually intended to facilitate travel or to meet the needs of morning meals at home. Taxing them at 20 per mille, on par with luxury goods, is not fair. (2) The sales channels are narrow, and the transaction value is only a few cents to a few dimes, never exceeding a few dollars. The tax rate for the sundries industry is only 5 per mille. Comparing the two, a rate of 1 per mille would be more appropriate to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. (3) Tea and snack stores, in addition to homemade pastries which should be taxed, also sell side items such as pickled vegetables, canned goods, and candies. When the tea and snack industry accepts these items from other industries, they have already been taxed and paid within the purchase price. If the tea and snack industry is taxed again when selling them, it is no different from taxing the same item twice, which is almost double taxation. (4) The resolution of the Five Provinces' Abolition of Levies Conference states that silk taxes should be refunded for silk thread taxes, and silk thread taxes should be refunded for cocoon taxes, in order to avoid double taxation. The items sold by the tea and snack industry have one item that combines three taxes (consolidated tax, special tax, and factory tax), which is too numerous to list. They should not be taxed at the highest business tax rate. (5) The provincial government's business tax regulations tax the snack industry at only 2 per mille. The difference in tax rates is more than ten times, which is a large discrepancy and inconsistent with the Ministry's Outline of Business Tax Regulations. Based on the above five points, our industry's commercial activity is minor, and the market is depressed. In terms of the situation, we are unable to bear the tax burden. Considering that citizens should contribute to government expenses, but compared with the tax rates of the rice, salt, sundries, and snack industries, this is unfair. Even in terms of taxation, we should follow the Ministry's Outline of Business Tax Regulations and deliberate on the matter. Since our city has no loss from the abolition of levies, this business tax should be postponed to alleviate the people's difficulties and revitalize commerce. If it is necessary to implement it, foreign and Chinese stores should be treated equally. Our association is deeply concerned and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we respectfully submit our difficulties to your esteemed association, requesting you to forward them to the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Government for reconsideration to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. We would be truly grateful.” (Below omitted)

Xin Chang Shipowner Requests Maritime Trial 90

▲ Central Cabin Ruptured, Water Submerged Deck

Inspect Bottom First Before Salvage

▲ Shipowner Returns to Shanghai The news that the China Merchants Bureau's Xin Chang ship ran aground near Ma'anshan and that the crew and sailors were rescued by the Bureau's dispatched ship has already been reported in this newspaper. The Xin Chang shipowner, Mr. Sha Deng, along with the chief mate, second mate, chief engineer, and steward, waited for the chief shipowner, Mr. Mackner, to arrive and inspect the ship. Therefore, they were the last to leave the ship. Sha Deng and the other four left the ship at 3:00 AM on the 7th, boarded the Lijin warship, and returned to the Xin Chang ship with the chief shipowner on the 8th. At 11:00 AM, they boarded the Xuepu Sun barge and returned to Shanghai at around 7:00 PM that night. Yesterday, Sha Deng and the chief mate, Zhao Shimei, went to the Bureau to report the details of the Xin Chang accident to the General Manager, saying that this disaster was caused by unavoidable natural disasters. They reported in detail the moment the ship encountered fog and waves that drove it into the hidden reef, confirming that it was an irresistible maritime disaster. They then went to the Shipping Department to discuss the salvage plan with Chief Huang, where a precise consultation was held.

▲ Arbitrating Responsibility The shipowner and chief mate were on duty together when the Xin Chang ran aground. Now, in order to clarify the responsibility for this accident, Mr. Sha Deng has submitted a request to the Bureau, requesting the Jianghai Customs Marine Survey Department and another maritime expert to organize a maritime court to hear the case in order to prove that it was indeed a natural disaster and not the fault of the shipowner or crew. General Manager Li will comply with Sha Deng's request and submit the issue of responsibility to trial to ensure fairness.

▲ Crew Requests The crew and sailors who arrived in Shanghai yesterday sent representatives to the Bureau to request compensation for losses. General Manager Li sent Mr. Zhu to receive and comfort them, promising to retain the positions of all employees, give priority to arranging employment, and provide each employee with 40 yuan to assist with their losses. The drowned mess boy, Mr. Dong, will be given a pension by the Bureau. The eight crew members who took a fishing boat to Ningbo are expected to arrive in Shanghai today.

▲ Suggestion of Salvage When the shipowner and others last left the Xin Chang, the ship was sinking into the water because the first two cabins were ruptured and the engine room was flooded. The seawater submerged the deck. Yesterday, the Shanghai agent of the Japan Tokyo Salvage Company sent personnel to the Bureau to discuss salvage procedures. The Bureau needs to examine this matter further. It was agreed yesterday to first borrow technicians and divers from the Jiangnan Shipyard to go to the scene of the accident and inspect the bottom of the Xin Chang before discussing salvage procedures. The technicians will depart today.

▲ Requesting Warship Protection The Haijun Yuzhang warship has not yet reported, but four fishing boats have already boarded the ship after the crew left and looted the ship's contents, including the crew and sailors' luggage, clothes, money, and sundries. When the chief crew arrived at the ship for inspection, everything had already been taken away. Yesterday, the Bureau urgently telegraphed the Xiamen Navy, requesting them to send marines to protect the ship to prevent pirates from damaging machinery and screws.

▲ Comprador Loss The comprador, Sheng Wunian, previously lost over 1,000 taels of gold on the ship while transporting a group of people from Guangdong and Guangxi. Afterward, his request for compensation was approved by the Beijing authorities but has not yet been issued. Now that the ship has been wrecked, the comprador's losses are also significant. He has placed the personnel of the cargo handling department under the Bureau's control.

▲ Hong Kong Service Suspended The Xin Chang was the best ship of the China Merchants Bureau and could travel to Hong Kong and carry passengers. Now that it has been wrecked, although the Bureau has many ships, none can be used for the Hong Kong route. Therefore, the Shanghai-Hong Kong route will be temporarily suspended. It is said that General Manager Li is already considering this.

Silk Factory Industry Held Another Meeting Yesterday 92

▲ Still Pushing Wang Xu and Two Representatives to Petition in Beijing

The Special Relief Committee for the Silk Industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai held a plenary committee discussion meeting yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM because the representatives who went to Beijing regarding the silk industry public bonds had returned to Shanghai. More than ten people attended, chaired by Shen Huachen. After performing the formalities, the chairman announced the purpose of the meeting. Wang Xiaolai, one of the representatives who went to Beijing, reported on the situation in Beijing, saying that they had successively visited Chairman Zhuang and the Ministers of Finance and Industry, and hosted banquets for the members of the Legislative Yuan. The results of the petition were quite satisfactory, and all agreed to reconsider. Next, Representative Chu Ziseng reported on the reason for the reduction in the amount issued. Minister Kong said that when the public bonds were requested, the price of middle-grade silk was only 800 taels. Subsequently, Director Zou of the Commodity Inspection Bureau reported that the price of silk had risen to 1,070 to 80 taels, and the silk factory industry did not need huge relief funds, so it was changed to encourage exports, improve locomotives, and improve sericulture, each issuing 2 million yuan. However, the good silk price lasted less than a week and returned to around 1,000 taels. The factory's capital still needs to be net 1,000 taels less. Adding the cost of reeling labor and interest, the total cost of middle-grade silk is 1,300 taels. Selling at market price, the factory needs to lose 200 to 300 taels. Furthermore, most silk factories in the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai are still closed. The factories that are open are all borrowing from the financial sector to start machines. Because of the mortgage relationship, waiting for relief is extremely urgent. Next, Committee Member Wu said that the government may have misunderstood the locomotive improvement section. Most manufacturers everywhere rent car reeling silk, accounting for 90%. Improving locomotives should be the responsibility of the factory owner, not the manufacturer. The word "reward" is inversely proportional to the word "relief." Rewards do not require clearing debt principal and interest. Now, the silk industry public bonds must require manufacturers to clear debt principal and interest separately, which is purely a relief nature. The word "reward" is not applicable and should be corrected. Finally, the committee members repeatedly discussed that there are about 50,000 silk cars in the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai. The factories are closed, waiting for relief, and they are all in a hurry. 4 million yuan is not enough to distribute. It was decided that Wang Xu and two representatives should still be pushed to take a train to Beijing on the same day to present to the National Government, maintain the original plan, issue public bonds of 8 million yuan, use 2 million yuan to improve prudent medicine, and use 6 million yuan to relieve the silk factory industry. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM.

Congsha Six Ship Joint Alliance Established 94

▲ Jufeng Ship Plans to Sell and Suspend Service

▲ Xin Renhe Also Joins Service

▲ Conference and Joint Management The six Congsha shift companies have been competing too fiercely, and their losses last year were quite large. This year, Da Xing, Xu Zhongxin, and others initiated the establishment of an alliance and cooperation, following the example of the Ningbo and Taizhou routes. Representatives from the six companies held a meeting at the Shipping Industry Association and unanimously agreed to cooperate. They then discussed the joint management conditions, and Liu Bingsheng, the representative of Jufeng Company, proposed to withdraw the Haimen ship from the route.

▲ Purchase Haimen Jufeng Company had long planned to abandon the Congsha line and switch to another route. This matter was mentioned last year. The other five companies on the line planned to accept the company's ships, so they discussed the matter. According to the five companies' proposal, the Jufeng Company's Haimen ship would be jointly purchased by the five companies, and the ship price would be bought at the 36,000 yuan set last year. Liu Bingsheng said that the ship price issue requires a slight request from the shareholders for consent before a decision can be made. It was heard yesterday that the Jufeng shareholders believe that the price is too short, so they are still in negotiation.

▲ Organize Association Congsha joint management has been agreed by Da Xing, Da Da, Ping An, Xin Xing Long, and others to organize an association. Each company sends staff to join the association to handle affairs, and the Congsha shift ships are completely handed over to the association for management. All matters such as dispatching shifts, freight rates, and cabin positions are subject to the full discretion of the association. The number of ships leaving port each day is reduced from four to two. Once the purchase of the Haimen ship is resolved, it will be implemented. At that time, passenger feet will still return to their original state. The five companies are currently in the process of preparing.

▲ Renhe Joins The Xin Renhe ship also operates on the Congsha shift. In order to improve the ship and increase cabin space, the company had the ship repaired in the shipyard and renovated it. Once it is completely completed, it will join the association and travel on the Congsha route with the six companies. Yesterday, the reporter met someone in the association and inquired about the situation. According to reports, it can be established and implemented in cooperation within half a month at the latest.

Measures of the Social Bureau to Ban Various Savings Stores 96

▲ Appoint Accountants to Investigate and Report

▲ Yonghua and Lihua are also in the process of banning

The Social Bureau, according to the order transferred by the Municipal Government to the Ministry of Finance to ban ordinary companies and shops from operating savings, has previously ordered various companies and shops to end and report within one month, the details of which have been reported in this newspaper many times. It is now heard that after the companies and shops were ordered, they are all willing to end the savings department in accordance with the order, but the methods of proceeding are different. For example, Yong'an branch is reorganizing the bank, Sincere Company has changed the savings accounts to deposit accounts or current accounts, and China Underwear Weaving Factory has set a period to send away savings, but only the Sino-Western Sino-French Women's Virtue Savings Association jointly organized by the two families has not yet reported the closing method. It is now heard that the Social Bureau believes that the methods of various savings companies and shops are very inconsistent, so they have ordered them as follows: (1) Order to stop collecting money immediately. (2) Ordinary shops that do not use the name of savings for deposits may be temporarily exempt from banning, but they still need to ask the central government for instructions. (3) Demand deposits must be sent away to each depositor within one month. (4) Time deposit methods are divided into two categories: A. If the depositor voluntarily withdraws money within one month, they should be allowed to change the interest to current account calculation in accordance with bank practice, and send away the deposit. B. If the depositor does not withdraw, the total amount should be transferred to a bank approved to handle savings, otherwise a considerable guarantee must be provided to the Central Bank to temporarily wait for the central government to approve. (5) Entrust an accountant to check the total amount of various savings deposits, business conditions, and asset and liability status of each company and shop within one week, and report for approval. The above-mentioned methods of decision have been reported to the municipal government for record.

Also, Yonghua Company on Fada Road, Lihua Company on Paobou Road, and Jiufu Company on Baker Road, which usually operate savings, have also been ordered to close within one month.

Minutes of the Pushan Villa Board Meeting 97

▲No matter how difficult

▲We must strive to proceed

The Pushan Villa of Zhabei held a board meeting at its general office at No. 2, Sixth Avenue yesterday at 4:00 PM. Board members Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Lu Weiyong, Shen Xiechen, Shi Gengyin, Chen Liangyu, and Wang Junsheng were present. Chairman Wang Yiting opened the meeting as usual, followed by a report from Director Wang Junsheng on the various charitable deeds carried out in the 19th year. However, in recent years, the area has become vast, the exposure to the elements has increased, materials and labor are expensive, and expenses are high. It is estimated that the budget for this year's expenses will be far from sufficient. Huang Hanzhi then stated that the charitable deeds carried out by the Villa are painstakingly and meticulously done, leaving no effort unspared, and are beneficial to the public health and the diseases of the poor. No matter how exhausted the funds or how difficult the operation, efforts must be made to proceed and find ways to raise funds to ensure sustainability. Everyone agreed and resolved that the directors and members of the Villa, who have always been charitable and enthusiastic about helping others, should discuss the financial difficulties and solicit generous donations to maintain the charitable cause. Continued Trial of the Inducement and Adultery Case of the Young Owner of a Sock Factory 100

▲Where did Shen Meimei's son come from?

▲Zhong Xiaoqi is still trying to deny it

▲Sentencing scheduled for next Monday

Zhong Xiaoqi, the young owner of a Guangdong sock factory, had an intimate relationship with his neighbor Shen Meimei in September two years ago, and they had a close relationship and secretly made a lifelong commitment. When Shen Meimei became pregnant and gave birth to a child, she was abandoned by Zhong. Shen's mother, Shen Li, hired lawyer Shen Xingxia to sue Zhong for inducement and adultery in the Special District Local Court. The court has heard the case several times, and the details have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, the hearing was held again. Judge Xiao Xiefen opened the Fifth Court to summon both plaintiffs and defendants and their representatives, who arrived on time to await the hearing. The details of the trial are recorded below:

▲Prostitute arrives in court and then withdraws Judge Xiao had not yet begun the questioning when the defendant's lawyer, Ye Dikang, first stated that of the witnesses summoned by the court, the prostitutes Ai Yue and Qing Feng, only Qing Feng had arrived today, but soon disappeared again, perhaps at the instigation of the plaintiffs. Zhong Xiaoqi also added that it was lawyer Shen who ordered her to go back. Lawyer Shen replied that his firm did not know Qing Feng and that the plaintiff's lawyer could not order the defendant's witnesses to go anywhere. Opening rooms mostly during the day Judge Xiao then questioned Shen Meimei, asking when she came to Shanghai. Shen replied that she had been in Shanghai for seven or eight years. He asked who she lived with in Shanghai. She replied that she lived with her mother and sister-in-law. After marrying her sister-in-law, her mother returned to Suzhou. He asked when her sister-in-law died and when her mother came to Shanghai. She replied that her sister-in-law died in October last year and her mother came in September. He asked if she and Zhong Xiaoqi opened rooms or borrowed houses. She replied that they opened rooms and never borrowed houses. He asked if they opened rooms during the day or at night. She replied that it was during the day, and she was always at home at night. He asked how many times they opened rooms in total. She replied that he often asked her to go, and she couldn't remember how many times. He asked when it started. She replied that it started on September 23 of the year before last. He asked if her mother was in Shanghai at the time. She replied that she was in Suzhou. She said she came back to Shanghai for a funeral. He asked when her mother found out. She replied that she only found out in September last year.

▲Pu Laosi submits a statement as a witness At this point, Judge Xiao asked if the witnesses had arrived. A Chinese constable No. 1281 reported that he had been ordered to summon the two prostitutes Ai Yue and Qing Feng. The first time he went to summon them, both prostitutes refused to accept the summons. The second time he went to summon them, they both accepted, but he didn't know if they had arrived today. Lawyer Shen immediately said that Ai Yue's mother had arrived. Judge Xiao then summoned Ai Yue's mother, Pu Laosi, for questioning. Pu Laosi stated that she was 39 years old, the mother of Ai Yue, and the owner of the brothel, currently residing in Minhe Lane. Judge Xiao instructed her to tell the truth when testifying in court, otherwise she would be punished. He then ordered Pu Laosi to sign a statement, pointed at Shen Meimei, and asked if Pu Laosi knew her. Pu replied that she did not know her. He asked if she had ever done business at her place. She replied that her family was all her own people and there were no outsiders, so she didn't know this person.

▲Shen Meimei cries for fourteen days Judge Xiao then asked Shen Meimei's mother, Shen Li, when she married her daughter-in-law. She replied that she married her daughter-in-law on April 19 last year. He asked if she was often in Shanghai before marrying her daughter-in-law. She replied that she was often in Shanghai, but after marrying her daughter-in-law, she often returned to Changzhou. He asked if she knew that her daughter and Zhong Xiaoqi opened a room on September 23 of the year before last. She replied that she was often sick at the time, and when her daughter went out during the day, she always excused herself by saying that she was going to Huajin Lane to buy goods, and she never stayed out at night, so she didn't pay attention and didn't know. He asked when she found out later. She replied that in October last year, she came to Shanghai from Suzhou and saw that her daughter was pregnant. After asking, she said that it was the young owner next door who was the father, and that the young owner had expressed his willingness to marry her daughter. Later, she was abandoned by the young owner and did not care for her. Therefore, when her daughter gave birth at Guangren Hospital, she cried for fourteen days and became seriously ill, so much so that she has not yet recovered. Even today, when going upstairs to await the hearing, she needs two people to support her.

▲Zhong Xiaoqi's denial Judge Xiao turned to Zhong Xiaoqi and asked if he opened a room with Shen Meimei during the day or at night. He replied that it was both day and night, but he only stayed overnight once, and her mother knew about it. Her mother also said to him that opening rooms outside was too uneconomical and asked him to live in her house to save money. Her family runs a club, so he can play cards and smoke. Her mother has also lived in Shanghai for a long time, and her mother buys the groceries every day. The court doesn't believe it, you can investigate in the alley and you will understand. At this point, Lawyer Shen, with the permission of Judge Xiao, asked Zhong if Shen Meimei's child was his. Zhong replied that it was not his. She is a prostitute and has many customers, so of course he doesn't know who the father is. He also asked that, since it was not his child, why did he send her to Guangren Hospital? Zhong replied that he did not send her. Lawyer Shen immediately stated to the court that his firm had entrusted Lawyer Yang to send a letter to Guangren Hospital to inquire whether there was a woman named Zhong who came to the hospital to give birth. He now has a reply from the hospital, stating that a woman named Zhong did come to the hospital to give birth and was sent by a Guangdong sock factory. He then presented the reply to the court. Then he questioned Zhong Xiaoqi again, asking what he meant by the sentence in the letter he wrote to Shen Meimei, "I harmed you for life in the past, and I will repay you in the future, and I cannot forgive you even in death." Zhong said he did not want to answer. Lawyer Shen then said to Zhong, you must tell the truth. Zhong replied that if he told the truth, Shen Meimei would not have sued him in court. At this point, the defendant's lawyer, Ye Dikang, stated that the photo of Shen and Zhong taken together that was published in the newspaper a few days ago was created by the plaintiff by pasting her own photo with Zhong's photo, because the defendant had never taken a photo with the plaintiff.

▲Closing arguments and sentencing scheduled Judge Xiao ordered the closing arguments to begin. After mutual vigorous arguments by lawyers Shen and Ye, the court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for 2:00 PM on Monday of next week. He then asked Zhong Xiaoqi if he had anything to say. Zhong replied that Shen Meimei was indeed a prostitute and asked the court to investigate thoroughly so that it would be clear. If the investigation showed that she was not a prostitute, he would willingly be punished twice as much. After giving his statement, he left the court.

Reducing the Price to Sell a Daughter is Strange 102

▲Uncle and nephew don't know each other

▲Is there any doubt about trafficking in human beings?

Pu Mingyuan, a 40-year-old man from Nanjing, has been running a Pu Hengtai tooth sign shop at No. 6 Jianyuli, South Street, Hai Chao Temple, outside Xiaonanmen in Nanshi. At around 3:00 PM yesterday, a man resembling a worker brought a girl to Pu's shop, saying that if anyone wanted the young girl, they only needed to pay 160 yuan. Pu said he didn't want her. Then the man suddenly lowered the price to 100 yuan. Pu thought that the sale of the young girl must be of unknown origin and suspicious, so he told him to wait a moment and secretly went out to call the watchman police officer Wu Yanyi of the 26th post to come and arrest him, and took the young girl to the 1st District, 3rd Precinct. During the preliminary interrogation, Chief Jin asked the man, who gave his name as Wu Zhicheng, 30 years old, from Yancheng, Jiangbei, who made a living by pulling a rickshaw and currently lived at No. 7, Lane 3, Yanpingli, Jiaxing Road, Nanshi. He said that his brother Zhifu's wife, Xu, gave birth to a daughter (the young girl Yang brought). Zhifu died many years ago. Because Xu had no way to make a living in the countryside, she took the girl to Shanghai to make a living. Unexpectedly, Xu suddenly eloped with someone a few days ago, leaving the girl unattended. He planned to take her back to his hometown, but he completely denied selling the girl. When asked, the young girl stated that her name was Si Yatou, she was nine years old, from Jiangbei, and her parents were both alive at home, and she also had a younger brother named Daqiuzi. She said that she did not know this man (referring to Wu). The chief thought that there was no reason why an uncle and nephew would not know each other, and it was clearly a case of trafficking in human beings. He ordered him to be detained for investigation.

Yao Liankui is Daring 104

▲Forging an Order from the Supreme Court

▲Using a small wooden seal to create a square seal

▲Fraudulent under the name of a process server

▲Not repenting even after serving three years

Yao Liankui, also known as Yao Zhengkun, from Anhui, once impersonated a clerk of the Local Court and stole and sold the bricks and tiles of the court, and defrauded litigants of money. He was punished by the court for three years. After being released, he did not restrain himself and continued to swindle and deceive others.

Lu Zhang, a woman from the Laobaidu area of ​​Pudong, was detained due to her husband's debt case. Yao acted as her guarantor. In civil cases, no matter what, bail must be allowed, and there is no need to find a way. However, Yao deceived her because she was a woman and defrauded her of 52 yuan under the guise of a process server. The woman later inquired from the original process server, Mao Shukang, who said that there was no such thing. The woman told her to go to court to file a complaint. Yesterday morning, the woman brought Yao to the court, and the process servers on duty, Xu Qingxi and Zhai Jinwen, sent him to the prosecutor's office to report. Police Chief Xu Jinqing and Police Inspector Chen Xihui, based on Lu Zhang's claim that Yao had forged documents with him, ordered bailiff Li Jiajun and others to search out two forged official documents: (1) An order from the Supreme Court. The forged paper was a civil mediation document purchased from the Special District Court for five cents. A small wooden seal was used to create a square seal, with the words "Order Ma Daoyu to pay the litigation fee of 12 yuan and 5 cents in this case. Pay immediately and do not delay. This is important. Yu's share of the litigation fee in this case is nine-tenths. Pay immediately and do not resist. Those who violate this order will be punished. This order is for Ma Daoyu. January 28, Year 20. Appeal rejected. The appellant, Lu Yu, is informed. Judge Pang Zhen of the Supreme Court." (2) The paper was a report paper from the court, with the words "Shanghai Special District Local Court's application for reconsideration of a case, for reporting matters. Two documents, No. 130, Shangzi, Year 19. Received Ma Daoyu's fee for applying for reconsideration, 2 yuan and 55 cents. Judge Gong, Clerk's Seal." When asked about the seal, he also used a small wooden seal to cover more than ten times, forming a square seal. The handwriting was terrible and unprecedented. Moreover, the above-mentioned forged official documents can truly be said to be incomprehensible, making people laugh when reading them. It can only deceive illiterate rural fools. However, his boldness and recklessness are already evident. Therefore, it was immediately reported to Chief Prosecutor Liu Maochu, who entrusted Prosecutor Yang Wenjun to open a court for preliminary trial. Yao was deemed to have committed serious crimes and was ordered to be detained pending prosecution.

▲Learning to drive a car collides with a streetcar

▲Traffic was cut off for more than half an hour

At 5:45 PM yesterday, at the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Rue Mercier in the French Concession, the French streetcar No. 24 on Route 2, operated by a French company, heading from the Bund to Xujiahui, was stopped to drop off passengers when a sedan-style car with Concession registration No. 206 and Chinese registration No. 6231 suddenly drove head-on. Repercussions of the Installment Repayment Plan for the Riye Bank Case 107

▲The Social Affairs Bureau has rejected the plan based on the circumstances

The method for repaying debts of the Riye Bank and the Great World Savings Department in this city was proposed by Min Caizhang, the manager of the Great World, and submitted to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for adoption and implementation. It has been reported in detail in this newspaper. It is now reported that the Social Affairs Bureau has rejected the plan based on the opposition of the debtors Diao Qianjin, Li Shenji, Li Shiji, and others. The reasons are roughly as follows: Most of the creditors are from the lower and middle classes of society, and all their meager savings are relied on for their current livelihood. If they are cunningly delayed in this way, it is feared that most of the creditors will be reduced to poverty within a year, and how can they survive? As for the various businesses of the Gongfa Company, it is difficult to guarantee that there will be no changes in the recent business within a few years. How can they wait for thirty years? If this statement is implemented, it is tantamount to strangling the creditors to death. For the present plan, the existing assets of the Gongfa Company should be urgently disposed of as soon as possible. If the amount is insufficient, the sons of Chu Jiu and all the shareholders should be strictly ordered to bear unlimited liability. A quick and decisive approach should be taken to end this case in the shortest possible time. Therefore, the Social Affairs Bureau believes that this method is too disadvantageous to the depositors and has rejected it based on the circumstances.

A Westerner Overturns His Car on a Road Illegally Built Outside the Concession 108

▲Did not report to the Public Security Bureau after the accident

The Westerner, Forsell, was driving his car No. 8955 at 11:30 PM the night before last when he collided with truck No. 16826 on Columbia Road, which was illegally built outside the Concession by the Public Works Department. The car overturned on the ground. Forsell abandoned the car on the road and returned to Shanghai, hiring workers from the Niupan Automobile Repair Shop to transport it. However, the accident site was in the Chinese territory. The Westerner did not report to the Sixth District, Second Precinct Public Security Bureau at the time. Therefore, the Chinese police prevented Forsell from acting without authorization. Forsell was unable to do anything and returned empty-handed. Later, the head of the Jing'an Temple Police Department explained everything to Chief Liu of the Sixth District, Third Precinct Public Security Bureau, and the Westerner was allowed to transport the car away.

Zheng Zizhang's Car is Found 109

▲A kidnapping case occurred in the Concession

▲Should be notified to the Chinese territory at any time

▲May be intercepted in case of an emergency

Zheng (wrongly written as Chen in yesterday's newspaper) Zizhang, a Teochew native who lived on Haining Road in the Public Concession and opened a Hoji pawnshop, was kidnapped by bandits in front of the house of a foreign prostitute at No. 29 Shantou Road at 0:30 AM yesterday, and disappeared without a trace. The details have been reported in this newspaper. However, Zheng's private car was also taken away by the bandits at the same time and could not be found. Until about 2:00 AM yesterday, a black-plated, self-provided green sedan car suddenly stopped at the intersection of Dalin Road and Fangxie Road in the jurisdiction of the Second District Headquarters of Nanshi. The front of the car was facing north, the Concession number was 4633, and the city number was 5695. There was originally post No. 23 set up there, but it was moved to the back road of the Manufacturing Bureau. Police officer Cheng Maoqing discovered the car. After carefully inspecting the car, he found that there was no one in it. After waiting for a long time, he asked the nearby residents, who said that a car suddenly came a while ago, and three people jumped out and went east. The police officer immediately reported to the Second District Headquarters. When District Chief Wang heard the news, he ordered the car to be detained and telegraphed the Public Works Bureau. According to the reply, the car belonged to a Zheng family of Hoji pawnshop on Haining Road. District Chief Wang further inquired from the pawnshop, who said that the car was stolen on Simalu at 12:00 PM and did not mention the kidnapping. It was not until District Chief Wang reviewed the newspaper yesterday morning that he learned the truth. He immediately telegraphed the Supervision Office and notified the Laozha Police Department. The police chief sent Western Detective Kemin and Detective Cui Jinchuan to the Second District Headquarters to request the army to lead them back for investigation. District Chief Wang declared to the Western detective that since a kidnapping case had occurred in the Concession, the car number should be telegraphed to the Chinese police authorities at any time so that they could pay attention to it everywhere and possibly intercept it in case of an emergency. He hoped that in the future, there would be no distinction between boundaries, and that they would communicate with each other in the spirit of mutual assistance to achieve rapid results. The Western detective was quite moved by the words and expressed his apologies in person, taking the car back.

The Chinese Child Welfare Association sends a letter requesting a thorough investigation of child trafficking organizations in Nanshi 111

The Chinese Child Welfare Association sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau yesterday, stating, "Respectfully, we have recently received reports from various sources stating that child traffickers are often found on the streets of Nanshi, specializing in luring and abducting boys and girls, secretly hiding them in organizations organized by the traffickers. They even change their names and teach them how to address people. Once the training is completed, they are trafficked to other places and sold at a high price. In recent days, the number of children who have been abducted and lost has increased. Please take steps to rescue them." According to investigations, the loss of children has indeed been heard daily. If no measures are taken to rescue them, the protection of children will be lost. Our association is a child welfare organization, so we dare to send this letter to urge your bureau to issue a strict prohibition, send more detectives to investigate everywhere, and order all districts to pay attention at all times. Once discovered, they should be severely punished to maintain humanity and restrain the bandits. We believe that your bureau attaches importance to public security and will grant our request."

Candle Industry Guild Decides to Raise Prices 112

▲ Effective from the 19th

The Shanghai candle industry guild has received reports from various members stating that due to tariff increases on materials such as asphalt and beeswax, prices have been rising daily. Continuing to purchase at the previous prices would result in losses and make it difficult to sustain operations. Therefore, a special meeting was requested and a resolution was made to increase prices and notify all members to maintain costs and benefit operations. The guild convened a general meeting of representatives yesterday, with a large attendance. Shen Cheng Zhang was elected chairman. After discussion, it was decided that starting from the 19th of this month, the wholesale prices would be: for Da Tong Hang, 41 yuan per dan; for Xin Tong Hang, 40 yuan per dan. The retail price would be 4 jiao 8 fen per jin. Strict adherence is required. Anyone found to be outwardly compliant but secretly selling at lower prices will be investigated upon report, and dealt with according to the established regulations. The resolution was passed.

Copper Worker Dies Tragically at Jiu Feng Silk Factory 115

▲ Clothes Entangled in Machine Belt

▲ Right Hand Crushed and Death from Being Rolled into the Machine

Jiang Lian Gui, a 23-year-old copper worker from Shaoxing at the Jiu Feng Silk Factory on Zhongxing Road in Zhabei, started work at 7 a.m. on the 7th. While adding oil to the machine, he was momentarily careless, and his clothing became entangled in the overhead belt, causing him to be pulled into the machine. His right hand was crushed. After the machine was stopped, Jiang had already fainted from the pain. The factory hired a car to take him to Bao Long Hospital, but he died from his injuries at 10 a.m. The body was taken by the police to the Forensic Examination Office on Fei Lun Road. Yesterday morning, the Special District Local Court commissioned Prosecutor Guo to the office to clarify the circumstances of the death. He instructed the deceased's uncle, Wang Bing Fa, to sign an affidavit to claim the body for coffin and burial.

Education News Highlights

Declaration of the Chinese Vocational Education Society 124

▲Revealing the Five Major Causes of National Crisis

▲Hoping the Government Will Implement the Fourteen Proposed Items

▲The Society Now Plans to Realize the Principle of People's Livelihood

Cai Yuanpei, Hu Shuhua, Liu Zhanen, and forty-two other experts from the Chinese Vocational Education Society Expert Conference, issued a statement yesterday, saying,

"Our colleagues in the Society have been diligently researching, promoting, and experimenting with vocational education for many years. We have always presented our humble opinions to the government and contributed to society without fear of trouble. Now that the war has ended and the country is unified, we should work together to realize the principle of people's livelihood and eliminate national crises in their infancy. The Society is holding an expert conference to gather ideas and consider carefully. The result of the meeting is a unanimous call to offer our experience to the government and society. We declare that China's social problems are becoming increasingly serious. After identifying the most prominent, there are approximately several aspects. People often say that the more developed general education is, the more unemployed there are. Although this is due to [omission] relations, it may not be entirely true. However, hundreds of thousands graduate from higher primary schools but cannot enter middle school, and middle school graduates cannot enter university every year. These people are scattered throughout society, achieving neither great nor small success. They have considerable knowledge, cultivating desires beyond ordinary people, but lack specific skills to enter society. What will they do? Filled with depression, it is self-evident whether they are beneficial or harmful to the country and society. This is one.

The difficulty of relieving mass unemployment is common in all countries, but it is even more so in China. According to the 1920 statistical report of the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center of the Society, 2,872 people were entrusted to find employment, including 738 domestic university graduates and 133 foreign university graduates. Those who received higher education eagerly seek work. It is so pitiful, but on the other hand, the job market demands expertise in one skill. Those with high degrees are avoided. Shanghai is the leading commercial port, and one can extrapolate the situation throughout the country. Social enterprises have been declining daily, and the supply and demand of talent are mismatched. How much loss has the country and society suffered? It is impossible to calculate. This is two.

China's new industries are just budding, and they are far more immature than neighboring countries. Factory workers are young and energetic, and their thoughts are easily changed. By the time they are older, their habits are deeply ingrained, and they are often affected by sluggishness. The efficiency of work decreases, and there is no hope of increasing production. Correcting their thinking and changing their environment, everything to prevent disorder and benefit industry, is the most urgent task at present. This is three.

Women's employment is not only related to the prosperity of the family, but also benefits the social organization. Chinese women have never considered employment as important. Our colleagues believe in equal rights for men and women to participate in government [omission] based on [omission] principles. Only by providing society and the country with ample service knowledge and skills can self-reliance and helping others be effective. Whether working outside or managing the family, appropriate training must be given at a suitable age. Whether this approach of emphasizing general education for women is suitable for China's current needs is a major question. This is four.

China is a country based on agriculture. Today, the major source of food and clothing relies heavily on foreigners. Leaving aside cotton goods, according to the 1919 customs report, the price of imported rice reached over 58.9 million taels, the price of imported wheat reached over 21.4 million taels, and the price of imported flour reached over 62.9 million taels. It is enough to make people tremble. Agriculture is not cultivated, and production is declining daily. Farmers' intelligence is not developed, and there is no way to improve their lives. With such poor, weak, ignorant, and disorganized farmers, who account for more than 85% of the country's population, to say that the country can stand in today's world is nonsense. If we do not take measures to remedy this situation, the consequences are unimaginable. This is five.

The above five points are all urgent and pressing serious problems. To solve them, we cannot rely on one side alone. The key is to rely on vocational education. According to the latest statistics, there are 1,139 middle schools in the country, of which only 149 are vocational schools, accounting for only 13%. There are 234,811 middle school students in the country, of which only 16,641 are vocational school students, accounting for only 7%. The gap between supply and demand is so large that it is no wonder that job seekers cannot find jobs and employers lament the lack of talent. For more than ten years, our colleagues have exhausted their words and pens, ashamed of their inability to help the people's livelihood. The actual facilities are also very limited. What can be seen in society includes industrial and commercial education, agricultural education, sericulture, sewing, and other vocational education for women, various vocational supplementary education, and guidance for further education, employment guidance, and job placement. All of these are only tests of the Society's function, trying to open up new paths for society. However, the song is not high and there are few who harmonize. The brave take the lead and are isolated. The cries of the people's poverty and the exhaustion of wealth are deafening. Our hearts ache at the futility of a drop in the bucket. Today, we can no longer contain ourselves. There are too many reckless elements. Someone at this conference reported that 90% of bandits are soldiers, and 90% of Communists are school graduates. The former clearly reveals the source of the rebellion, and the latter cannot bear the pain of school bankruptcy. What we see is what everyone sees, and our hearts are truly worried. We dare to offer our sincerity and earnestly hope that our government, which governs the country, and our society, in which we live, will implement the following in the shortest possible time:

(1) The Ministry of Education should unite with the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Transportation, and other ministries to form a committee. From the perspective of talent, each should propose practical methods to connect the supply and demand sides of their respective responsible affairs, so that the use and training of talent can be mutually beneficial. The provincial education departments and municipal education bureaus should also have the same union. (2) The difference between the amount of general education and vocational education needed in various places is very obvious. The establishment of general schools should be restricted and effectively reduced. Vocational schools that have not been established in various places should be planned and established as soon as possible. Those that have been established should strive to fill their content and increase efficiency. (3) The establishment of vocational schools in various places must be extremely linked to both education and vocation. Therefore, the following four types of schools are considered to be more effective: (A) establishing schools in rural areas by zoning; (B) vocational schools running their own agricultural, industrial, and commercial institutions; (C) vocational schools cooperating with vocational groups of the same nature; (D) vocational groups establishing vocational schools of the same nature. All of the above four types allow students to study and practice what they learn in reality. After completing their studies, they must be required to serve in practice for half a year or a year and obtain a certificate of achievement from the manager before being officially granted a diploma. This method should also be adopted for all purposeful education, such as normal schools. (4) Vocational schools should adopt the apprenticeship system of various countries, requiring students to practice for a certain period of time before receiving instruction. This not only develops work habits, but also allows them to learn what they practice, making it easier to increase their interest in the profession. (5) General middle schools in various places must also offer vocational subjects, so that some young people who cannot continue their studies after their group will be able to gain a foothold in society. (6) Industrial and commercial groups in various places should be requested by the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Industry to issue an order to organize supplementary education within a time limit to increase the service knowledge and skills of workers, so as to lay the foundation for the development and improvement of industry. (7) A considerable number of places must be designated to pilot rural improvement, with the aim of improving the individual lives of farmers, and then gradually promote it. The method of starting is to train agricultural education teachers on the one hand, and rural police on the other, so that the arms and fingers can be used effectively. (8) Women's vocational education must be promoted in many ways and facilities should be provided as much as possible. The principle should be to promote social service without hindering family life. (9) Teachers for vocational schools must be trained as soon as possible. Rather than setting up separate institutions or establishing vocational subjects in normal schools, it is better to attach vocational normal subjects to vocational schools that have achieved results. (10) The promotion of compulsory education in various places, whether in cities or villages, must establish a standard, that is, do not allow those who are educated to leave their inherent lives absolutely until they have developed their corresponding abilities, so as not to make compulsory education more developed and the social foundation more shaken. (11) Elementary schools should pay special attention to vocational cultivation and provide them with the basic knowledge and skills of the occupation. (12) All levels of education should uniformly implement labor in training to establish a foundation of respect for occupation in the psychology of young people and to enable them to obtain a more correct outlook on life. (13) Vocational guidance centers should be established in various places. The government should select locations, pilot them first, give them full investigation and guidance, and train vocational guidance personnel as soon as possible. (14) Request the central government to establish a policy of industrial and commercial protection and implement it effectively, so that industry can be fully developed, which will not only benefit the way out for talent, but also fundamentally eliminate the danger to the country's future. Our Republic of China really depends on it. The government is entrusted by the people, and society is composed of individuals. It should be able to consider the danger of the national situation and the sincerity of our foolish hearts, show sympathy, adopt our suggestions immediately, and look forward with anticipation. We hereby declare, hoping for your observation."

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Orders Reporting of Student Rosters 125

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education instructed the provincial experimental elementary schools, saying, "It has been found that the staff and student rosters of each school should be reported in accordance with the regulations after one month from the beginning of the semester for verification. This roster is not only used to examine the changes of staff and students in each school, but also used to verify during graduation, to show importance. It is now found that the Nantong Middle School Experimental Elementary School and the Xuzhou Middle School Experimental Elementary School have not reported for the previous semester, which is a long overdue and very negligent matter. Among the schools that have reported, some only report new students or do not divide by grade, which is too simple to be examined. Now that the second semester of this year has passed one month, the principals of each school should report the staff and student rosters of this semester, together with those that have not been reported in previous semesters, within half a month for verification. When creating the roster, new and old students should be listed in detail by name and grade, without omission. If there are any omissions, it will be rejected during the graduation process. In addition to the separate order, the principal of the school is instructed to comply with this order."

The Municipal Education Bureau instructed the schools in the city yesterday, saying, "It is hereby notified that the Municipal Government Instruction No. 7513 states that the Executive Yuan Jiang Dian [omission] that the General Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force has initiated a memorial service for the fallen soldiers who died fighting against the rebellion, which is scheduled to be held at the Capital Public Stadium for three days starting on the 10th of this month. It also stipulates that the whole country should follow the unified memorial service method and submit it to the National Government for approval. The main points are: (1) The memorial tablet for the fallen soldiers should be three feet wide and one foot five inches high, with the words 'The Tablets of Fallen Soldiers of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Who Died Fighting Against the Rebellion'; (2) All party, government, military, and school institutions, and all public and professional organizations in various places should gather at a spacious location in their respective localities at 8:00 a.m. on March 10th and hold a memorial service following the central ritual. All participants should wear black gauze armbands. All troops should also gather and hold a memorial service in their respective localities at the same time, or jointly with local organizations and groups; (3) The national army and navy should fire thirty-three commemorative salutes at 8:00 a.m. on March 10th. Where there are aircraft, they should be dispatched to fly and distribute propaganda; (4) All factories across the country should sound their sirens three times at 8:00 a.m. on March 10th; (5) The national flag should be flown at half-mast for three days and entertainment banquets should be suspended for one day; (6) All newspapers across the country should print the twelve characters 'In Memory of the Fallen Soldiers of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Who Died Fighting Against the Rebellion' on the first line of the front page, surrounded by a black border for one day. Record of the Establishment of the Chinese Linguistic Society 129

The Chinese Linguistic Society (The Linguistic Society of China), initiated by Chinese and foreign people in Shanghai, as reported by this newspaper on February 28, held its inaugural meeting on the afternoon of March 1 on the second floor of No. 23 Yuanmingyuan Road. The names of the executive committee members are as follows: President: Lin Hemin, professor of National Jinan University; Vice President: Dr. Chadli, chief engineer of Junpu; English Secretary and Treasurer: Fu Bulan, principal of Shanghai School for the Blind; Chinese Secretary: Zhong Luzhai; General Affairs Secretary: Ni Xiaoxian; and six reviewers: Shen Siliang, Fu Ruoyu, Zhu Wanxiang, Ji Muzuo Lin, Mo Anren, Wang Zhonghai, etc. The main promoters of the association are Chinese people, and there is no religious purpose. Cai Zimin and Lin Yutang of the Academia Sinica have also expressed personal interest in the association. The association hopes to pay attention to the following work: (1) Study the National Romanization promulgated by the National Government; (2) Promote the widespread use of Romanization in Shanghai, Ningbo, Taizhou, Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xinghua, Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, Hakka, and other places for phonetic notation and literacy, and to popularize mass education and study dialects in various parts of the country; (3) Promote the widespread use of phonetic symbols (omitted symbol); (4) Promote a perfect or phonetic shorthand; (5) Study Chinese Braille; (6) Study various other issues of Chinese language and writing. The association pays special attention to the National Romanization and phonetic symbols (omitted symbol). The association has purchased various Romanization and phonetic symbol (omitted symbol) books and placed them in the following libraries for free reference: (1) YMC A Library on the first floor of No. 23 Yuanmingyuan Road; (2) Hujiang University Library; (3) St. John's University Library; (4) Library of the Chinese Scientific Society, No. 533 Avenue Dubail, French Concession. Anyone who wants to join the association should pay a membership fee of two yuan. The association has several National Romanization and phonetic symbol (omitted symbol) pamphlets for members. The first public lecture of the association will be at 5:15 p.m. on Tuesday, March 17, with the topic "Chinese Language and Writing and Its Various Problems", and the speaker will be Dr. Mo Anren of the Shanghai Guangxuehui. Afterwards, there will be lectures on dialects in Shanghai, Ningbo, and other places and their Romanization. Anyone who wants to join the association or communicate can contact An Zhiyun at No. 418, No. 23 Yuanmingyuan Road.
